And I feel like the line in Purge the Poison describes this song pretty well! As far as I remember, from what I've read at the time Marina was out for success and not in a good place. Capitalism made her poor, but not in a monetary sense, more in a metaphorical one, as she always felt like she's the worst, not enough and not achieving her goals, at the time that could very well be meant in regards to her career. And I feel like that's true for a lot of people who desperately chase after money, as they feel that they find no value in themselves or their existence without it and that just makes a lot of people miserable. Especially when through social media you can continuously compare yourself to other people, even if only subconscious and see that they are way younger than you and more successful already. We all know that social media isn't reflecting reality 100% and people often make things look better than they truly are, but still comparing yourself to someone like that can make you feel like you failed at life and in a way make you poor in a figurative sense

Marina just never misses. So true queen
Grab a cuppa.  I think a part of me will always love Marina. I love how she sings about topical issues or reconfigures cliches into something more meaningful. But, the world right now is not as simplistic as this song (and Man's World) decry. There would be too much to go through right now, that seems a bit naive in this song (although sonically and visually it looks amazing), and that's because I'm dealing with a lot. But I'll say this... a woman, the new wife of my landlord appears to be making a heap of demands on my once kind landlord. And soon, I may be homeless. Homeless because she wants subway tiles or some shit. They're doing major renovations on both their million dollar properties and now they want to sell the rental I've lived in for twelve years. So, I've been calling the various homelessness resources, GOVERNED mostly by women, who are feeding me ice-cold attitudes and desensitisation (of which no sex is immune). And I'm dealing with a BArts degree at the best Uni in AUS, wondering if I'll be homeless. From "homeless to Harvard to homeless". I'm also dealing with health workers who are mostly women, as I have C-PTSD, and they aren't these shiny wonderful creatures just because they have a vagina.Some of them are fucking bitches from hell. Don't come at me because some guy pulled the wool over your eyes! Or fucked you over in some way. You aren't saints and angels yourselves. Most of you are manipulative, actually. I think it's important to remember that when someone has power, and there are a huge amount of societal sectors where that occurs (doesn't have to be politics), women are not immune to callousness. Plenty of women are in positions of power. It's not the government that will be helping me relocate, it's up to the woman in charge of my local homelessness organisation (the lovely anti-gay/ trans Salvation army) that my future and life is depending on. And it seems to me that rather than equalising the scales, the current feminist MO is to abuse men in a variety of ways, and to enable abuse. The abused becomes the abuser... As someone who was groomed by his mother to hate my father, making me feel like she was the victim of his alcoholism (and she was to a point). But beyond that simplistic picture, she was part of the problem. I have lived to protect my mum (was nearly killed by a machete by my dad) and other women in my life, only to come last on the list in homelessness shelters because some stoopid little girl got knocked up by some asshole and they get everything (because kids). On the streets I see mainly men that are homeless. In the small country town I moved to it's the women who have made life hard for me, with their gossiping ways. Do you know how damaging and destructive gossip can be? About to spend my 49th birthday alone tomorrow.  And this to someone who was sympathetic down to my core when it came to women. Now, I just see factions. Gender factions. But in reality, we can work together. Don't you know that 50% of women vote conservative? It's half of women that have created the problems other women now claim to be able to solve. It's all so naive. And it's GREED, not capitalism that is the problem. Why do people keep getting that wrong? I'm so tired of this century. Everyone is so dumb and making things worse. And the real problems go on. Women aren't creating a cultural revolution these days. Feminists did once, but not any more. The real questions you should be asking yourselves is... 1: How do you support men who support women? and 2: How to you deal with women who enable and support scumbag men? 50% of women voted for Trump, Johnson and Morrisson. What are you going to do about THEM?  So fucking get real and stop blaming my gender for all your problems. Take some responsibility for your life and where you position yourself. Britney had no problem being portrayed as a paedophilic sex symbol when she first came on the scene because she smelled the money and power. Now that she looks like a wreck, men are the problem. Pffff. She's just a dumbass.  Look, we've all been hurt. Focusing on the 0.0001% of men with actual power is basically retarded. And there are just as many women in power. Have they created utopia? In Germany? In New Zealand? NO. In New Zealand, indigenous people still suffer greatly, WITH A WOMAN IN CHARGE.   Are you getting the hint yet?  And for the record, this song shits on the lives of brave men and women (mainly MEN) who courageously fought in WWI and WWII against very real enemies. Millions paid with their lives for the freedom you take for granted. So, may God or whatever you believe in forgive YOU. We'd all be brainwashed Nazis if it wasn't for men. And yes, there have been unjust wars. So? Governments can be corrupt, like with Vietnam. Duh.  And where does this song talk about how people (men AND women) treat animals? THREE MILLION PEOPLE HAVE DIED AND ARE STILL DYING. Show me some real guts and take on traditional medicine and animal handling norms. Go on then! I mean, it's so glaringly missing from this song! The misery animals suffer should put all humans' problems to shame!  ANYWAY, I feel like Marina will continue to grow as an artist, and hopefully she will come to fully understand what women AND men deal with in this fucked up world. Just spare me the sugar and spice bullshit. And you're not solving problems, you're making things worse than they already are.     "Most people can bear adversity; but if you wish to know what a [person] really is give [them] power."  "Anger is a wind which blows out the lamp of the mind."  - Robert Green Ingersoll    P.S. I don't check the replies to my comments, so GO OFF. Enjoy your delusions! Enjoy the fact that there are women already destroying men's lives and favouring females. Think about my words when you see men on the streets, and pass them by. They must've done something to deserve it, right?! It's not health issues that put them there. It's karma!   We were healing. Men were learning. Things were changing.   Drive a wedge which will never be healed.

I like the music itself but I can't understand half of what she's saying and the lyrics I can hear clearly are boring and miserable. I don't have a problem with music being political. Madame X was a great album but this is predictable and dull. After Man's World (which I didn't mind), it seems like we're going to be getting a whole album dedicated to hating white men and much as I love Marina, I can't be bothered for that. I don't think men are perfect and I don't think women are perfect. Nobody is. Why can't these feminist anthems be like the Spice Girls songs and more about girl power than going on about the patriarchy and capitalism? I get that she has a message but it doesn't make for good or even enjoyable music.

some critical analysis of this video that i gleaned from my first viewing and a few listens of the song:  as for the song itself, i love how she takes on the voice of mother nature combined with the voice some omnipresent benevolent godhead just observing society and shaking its head at us all. this approach has been done before in media, but often it comes off as really preachy and self serving, whereas I feel like in this song the tone completely separates Marina the person from the speaker of the message which is being conveyed by Marina. the speaker comes off as sincere and well informed, so the listener can easily believe that this is coming from the perspective of a higher power and not just a person preaching or trying to prove that they are â€œwoke.â€  as for the video, the most obvious theme i noticed first and foremost is that in most of the video she is looking directly at the camera addressing the audience. and the camera is most often in a fisheye lens (moreso in the beginning), which reflects how human eyes see and process the world. so itâ€™s like sheâ€™s literally standing right in front of us, yelling at us how to fix the planet and our society, yet weâ€™re just speechlessly ignoring her message but still recognizing its existence by continuing to watch and stay close. the whole video feels like itâ€™s very intimate and interpersonal, like itâ€™s just you and her, and you both know each other all too well. and she isnâ€™t sad or desperate in her emotions, she is often smiling and dancing joyfully while still maintaining eye contact, but I think this is conveying her as mother nature continuing to live and thrive despite the damage that you, the viewer, has caused her. and even so, the proximity suggests that she is desperately trying to convey the message - her happiness being in defiance of your (societyâ€™s) hostility toward her.  as the video goes on, the fish eye shots appear less and the ones that replace them are wider and more traditionally voyeuristic shots that we are used to in a film or music video. and in doing so they also get dreamier, more blurred, and seem somewhat unreal. this is further enforced by all of the allusions to Dorothy in Oz (which imo feels a bit ham-fisted but it gets the message across to an audience that isnâ€™t necessarily looking for the more artistic/subtle ways of conveyance). and overall, feel like the message of this imagery is that we are all deluding ourselves - weâ€™re all living in this fantasy that everything is going to be okay and we can continue as we always have been, when everything is really falling apart right before our eyes. mother nature is literally treading water, she is begging for our help, and if we donâ€™t she was soon become weak and drown. we are choosing to be voyeurs instead of friends, backing away from that initial fish-eye interpersonal position to a place where we can comfortably view her in distress. we are at such a distance that we could claim that we can no longer reach out hand, but we are the ones who put ourselves in that position.   and again, even though Marina herself does not express emotions of distress on her face, her emotions in the pool are more subdued and stoic and then at the beginning of the video where she is clearly joyful. and combining that change of expression with the consistent repetition of â€œwho do you think you are?â€, even though her intonation doesnâ€™t change in the song itself, the question changes meaning as the video progresses.   in the beginning, itâ€™s more a question of: â€œweâ€™re friends, and what youâ€™ve done has really hurt me. can you recognize that your selfish actions have caused me harm?â€ itâ€™s a discussion where she is levelheaded and expressing her grievances; you are sitting across the table from each other, and she is informing you of your actions because she recognizes that you may not have realized you have hurt her; she is giving you room to apologize and repair the friendship.   near the middle, in the transitional period, it becomes: â€œwhy do you keep doing this? Iâ€™ve told you how much these actions have hurt me, and yet you are actively choosing to do so again and again. why do you think you can continue to treat me like this and I would be okay with it?â€ she is revealing a toxic pattern of behavior within your relationship where you are consistently hurting her but never apologize; you are her abuser. sheâ€™s also giving a kind of warning, that she will not tolerate such treatment for much longer, and that when she does eventually hit back, it will be justified and long overdue.  by the end, her saying â€œwho do you think you are?â€ is meant in the way we all know it to mean, in that disgusted, vitriolic tone that one would shout at a pompous asshole trying to take your seat at the table. here, she has truly run out of reasons to defend you, and no amount of empathy and understanding in the world can allow her to forgive you. you may have reasons for your actions, but they are not moral or defendable reasons; they are narcissistic and selfish in the truest sense of the word. she has told you time and again that you are hurting her and has given you far too many chances to make amends. yet you not only refuse to show remorse, you ratchet up the violence in response to her pleas, because when she does not obey you, it conflicts with your narcissistic view of yourself - you see yourself as deserving of everything in the universe, even if that means destroying it.  you are our society, who disrespects her beauty and grace; you are imperialism, capitalism, greed, structural inequality and discrimination; you are destruction incarnate.   you are poison. and now, after all this time, she is going to purge the poison.

New video of MARINA. As someone says in the comments: Show enormous energy and propose new artistic images with color included. Those women shoes in the water with the bubbles included are a natural-artificial artistic design. She breaks free of her conservatism to show sensuality, as befits a WORLDWIDE ARTIST like Shakira. Of course, this sensuality is demure because Marina has a British intellectual background. She shows naturalness, for example, her loose hair looks good on her. In my opinion, it is shown in this video that MARINA can be Young, although her face may not believe it, and renew herself as a woman, breaking her own pre-established rational limits.

I appreciate the feminist and pro-nature and anti-racism and anti-war verses, but I don't like how this is basically saying COVID is a punishment from nature. It is no better than the extremist religious people saying COVID is a punishment from God. It is insensitive to people who are suffering, & is making light of a tragedy that's killed millions of people and left millions more people traumatized.  Viruses don't come into fruition just because humans aren't good to the earth. All animals get viruses, not just humans. Many animals don't even live nearly as long as humans do. Like dogs live an average of 14 years before dying of natural causes. Is nature punishing them? I don't think so. I don't think nature is punishing humans, either.  Although I agree that humans should treat the earth better, this whole "nature is punishing humanity" is insensitive and untrue. We can advocate for better treatment of minorities & the earth without making light of a tragedy that's hurt and killed millions of people.  Edit: Also...the virus has hit minorities MUCH harder than it has hit privileged people. By this song's logic, nature would be punishing minorities harder than privileged people.  But the song also speaks against discrimination, which is good, so I don't think you would agree with that. So like I said, maybe it's better to get rid of the "covid is a punishment" entirely. It's not only nasty by itself, it can lead to even nastier implications (I actually have seen racists say that the virus has hit black people harder because black people are being punished by God).
Major Froot vibes (which has always been my favorite sound) packing punches like "Savages" with every line!  "Need to purge the poison, show us our humanity All the bad and good, racism and misogyny Nothing's hidden anymore, capitalism made us poor God, forgive America for every single war"
